كتاب البيع باب السلم
والـشـعـيــر والموزون المثمن ويصح في العددي المتقارب كـالـبـيـض والجوز والـفـلـس المداينة لما صححه الحاكم عن ابن عباس رضي الله تعالى عنهما قال : أشهد أن السلف المضمون إلى أجل مسمى قد أحله الله تعالى في الكتاب وأذن فيه قال الله تعالى يا أيها الذين آمنوا إذا تداينتم بدين إلى أجل مسمى فاكتبوه [البقرة: ۲۸۲] ومن السنة ما رواه الستة عن ابن عباس رضي الله تعالى عنهما قدم النبي الله والناس يسلفون في التمر السنة والسنتين والثلاثة فقال: من أسلم في شيء فليسلف في كيل معلوم ووزن معلوم إلى أجل معلوم» وهو على خلاف القياس إذ هو بيع المعدوم ووجب المصير إليه بالنص والإجماع للحاجة، ولا اعتبار بمن قال إنه على وفقه وقد أطال في الرد عليه في فتح القدير .
قوله : (ما أمكن ضبط صفته ومعرفة قدره صح السلم فيه لأنه لا يفضي إلى المنازعة. وفي القنية : السلم في العنب القلابي في وقت كونه حصر ما لا يصح، والسلم في التفاح الشامي قبل الإدراك يصح لأنه يسمى تفاحاً اهـ. وفي فروق الكرابيسي: بيع السلم يفارق بيع العين في ستة أشياء : خيار الرؤية وخيار الشرط ولو تفرقا يبطل، وفي إضافة السلم إلى الدراهم، وجعل الحنطة رأس المال على المختار وفي الأجل قوله: (وما لا فلا) أي وما لا يمكن ضبط صفته ومعرفة قدره لا يصح السلم فيه لأنه يفضي إلى المنازعة. ثم شرع يبين الفصلين بالفاء التفصيلية بقوله : فيصح) في المكيل كالبر والشعير والموزون المثمن كالعسل والزيت وفي الفروق الإسلام في الخبز وزناً يجوز اهـ. وفي القنية برقم (مع عك) أسلم زبيباً في كر حنطة لا يجوز وبرقم (حم عك) يجوز فأبو الفضل يجعل الزبيب كيلياً وهماً جعلاه وزنياً. والثوم والبصل يجوز السلم فيه وزناً لا عدداً، واللبن والعصير والخل يجوز كيلاً أو وزناً، ولا خير في السلم في الأواني المتخذة من الزجاج، وفي المكسور يجوز وزناً ؛ كذا ، البزازية. وفي الظهيرية ويجوز السلم في الدقيق كيلاً ووزناً ولو أسلم فلوساً في صفر أو سيفاً في حديد أو قصباً في بوار لا يجوز بخلاف ما لو أسلم قطناً في ثوب حيث يجوز اهـ. وفيها : لو أسلم في اللبن كيلاً أو وزناً جاز لأنه ليس بمكيل ولا موزون نصاً فيجوز كيفما كان. وشرط في الذخيرة رواج الفلوس أما إذا كانت كاسدة فإنه لا يجوز لأنه إسلام موزون
في المتن «ولو اشترى المسلم إليه كراً الخ (قوله ولا اعتبار بمن قال أنه على وفقه) أي على وفق القياس. قوله : (ولا خير في السلم في الأواني الخ) أي لا يجوز بل نفي الخيرية أدل على نفي الجواز؛ قاله بعض الشراح .
Book of sale, Chapter of salam. ... and barley, and weighed items that are prices. And it is valid in similar countable items like eggs and walnuts and the madā'ina fulūs (copper coins) because of what al-Ḥākim authenticated from Ibn ʿAbbās, may Allah be pleased with them, who said: I bear witness that guaranteed advance payment to a named term has been made lawful by Allah in the Book and permitted. Allah said: 'O you who have believed, when you contract a debt for a specified term, write it down' [Al-Baqarah 2:282]. And from the Sunnah, what the six narrated from Ibn ʿAbbās: The Prophet ﷺ came and people were paying in advance for dates for one, two, and three years, so he said: 'Whoever pays in advance for something, let it be in a known measure and a known weight to a known term.' And it is contrary to qiyās because it is a sale of a non-existent item, and recourse to it is obligatory by text and consensus due to need. No heed is given to whoever says it is consistent with qiyās, and al-Kamāl has extensively refuted him in Fatḥ al-Qadīr. His statement: (Whatever its description can be precisely defined and its quantity known, salam is valid in it because it does not lead to dispute.) In al-Qunyah: Salam in unripe black grapes at the time they are unripe is not valid, and salam in Syrian apples before ripening is valid because they are called apples, end. In Furūq al-Karābīsī: The contract of salam differs from the sale of a specific item in six things: option of inspection, option of stipulation, if they separate it becomes void, in adding salam to dirhams, and making wheat as capital on the chosen view, and in the term. His statement: (And what does not, so not) meaning whatever its description cannot be precisely defined and its quantity known, salam is not valid in it because it leads to dispute. Then he proceeds to explain the two categories with the detail letter fā', saying: It is valid in measured items like wheat and barley, and weighed items that are prices like honey and oil. In al-Furūq: Salam in bread by weight is permissible, end. In al-Qunyah number (with ʿak) if one pays raisins in advance for a kor of wheat it is not valid, number (ḥam ʿak) it is valid. So Abu al-Faḍl considers raisins as measured, while both (the others) considered them as weighed. Garlic and onion: salam in them is permissible by weight, not by count. Milk, juice, and vinegar: salam is permissible by measure or weight. There is no good in salam in vessels made of glass, and in broken pieces it is permissible by weight. Likewise in al-Bazzāziyyah. In al-Ẓāhiriyyah: Salam is permissible in flour by measure or weight. If one pays fulus (copper coins) in advance for brass, or a sword for iron, or cane for sulfur, it is not permissible, contrary to if one pays cotton in advance for a cloth, which is permissible, end. In it: If one pays in advance for milk by measure or weight it is permissible because it is not [explicitly] measured or weighed in the text, so it is permissible however it is. In al-Dhakhīrah, it is conditioned that fulus be in circulation, but if they are stagnant (out of circulation) then it is not permissible because it would be salam of a weighed item.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the general ruling on salam (advance payment sale). It begins by stating that salam is valid in various commodities: measured items like wheat and barley, weighed items that are prices (i.e., valuable metals like honey and oil), and similar countable items like eggs and walnuts. The proofs are from the Quran (verse 2:282) and the hadith of Ibn Abbas: the Prophet permitted salam in dates with known measure, weight, and term. The author notes that salam is contrary to qiyas (analogy) because it is a sale of a non-existent item, but it is permissible by text (Quran and hadith) and consensus due to the need of people. He dismisses those who claim it is consistent with qiyas, stating that al-Kamal ibn al-Humam has refuted them at length in Fath al-Qadir. The commentary then explains the condition for validity: the commodity must be capable of precise description and quantity measurement, to avoid dispute. Various examples are given from secondary works: salam in unripe grapes is invalid, but in unripe Syrian apples it is valid because they are identifiable. The passage then mentions six differences between salam and ordinary sale from al-Karabisi: option of inspection, option of stipulation, void if they separate after offer and acceptance, the addition of salam to dirhams, using wheat as capital (according to the chosen view), and the requirement of a fixed term. The text continues detailing specific rulings: garlic and onion are valid by weight only; milk, juice, vinegar by measure or weight; glass vessels invalid (broken glass by weight); flour by measure or weight; copper coins (fulus) must be in circulation. The author also notes internal Hanafi differences, e.g., over whether raisins are measured or weighed. Overall, the lesson establishes the framework of salam validity based on Quran, Sunnah, and consensus, emphasizing precise specification to avoid dispute.

Key Terms
السلم (al-salam): A contract of advance payment for a future delivery of a specified commodity.
المكيل (al-makīl): Commodities sold by measure (volume) such as grains.
الموزون المثمن (al-mawzūn al-muthamman): Weighed items that serve as prices (i.e., valuable commodities like gold, silver, but here used for honey, oil).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the permissibility of salam (advance sale) according to the text?
A) Qiyas on ordinary sale
B) Quran 2:282 and the hadith of Ibn Abbas
C) Istihsan alone
D) Ijma without textual proof

Key Takeaway
Salam is a valid contract in Hanafi fiqh, justified by Quran and Sunnah, provided the goods are precisely described and measurable to prevent dispute.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Salam in Money: Void or Valid as a Sale?
Resolves disagreement on salam in monetary metals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the competing Hanafi positions on salam in dirhams/dinars and apply the principle that a contract can be reclassified if its core objective is exchange.

Core Idea
Salam in dirhams is invalid, but the contract can be saved as a sale with deferred price.

What happens when you say 'salam' but use dirhams as the subject? Is the contract void or can it be reinterpreted? This lesson unpacks a classic Hanafi dispute between 'Isa ibn Aban and al-A'mash, and the later preference for al-A'mash's view that the contract becomes a valid sale. We'll walk through the arguments, analogies, and why this matters in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
Understand the scenario: a person pays a cloth (or other commodity) in advance for dirhams to be delivered later. Dirhams are thaman (price), not muthman (sold item).
Salam requires the price (ra's al-mal) to be paid in advance and the sold item delayed.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
'Isa ibn Aban holds the contract is void (batil) because it fails as salam and cannot be corrected. Al-A'mash holds it becomes a valid sale with deferred price.
Al-A'mash's view is preferred by later authorities like al-Kamal ibn al-Humam.
3
Analyze the proof for al-A'mash's view
Both salam and sale are exchanges of property (mubadala mal bi mal). The parties' objective is exchange; if the specific conditions of salam are missing, the contract can operate as a sale. The word 'salam' can also initiate a sale.
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defends this with analogies: partnership, gift/charity, agency.
4
Evaluate the opposing argument
'Isa ibn Aban argues the contract was intended exclusively as salam, so its failure voids the whole contract. The response: the common element of exchange allows reclassification.
Thamarah al-khilaf: under al-A'mash, the buyer gets dirhams after term; under 'Isa, the contract is annulled.
5
Apply the tarjih
The mufta bihi is al-A'mash's view: the contract is valid as a sale. This is based on the principle that legal transactions should be upheld as much as possible.
Even though the contract fails as salam, the core exchange is preserved.

متفاوت كالبطيخ والقرع والرمان والرؤوس والأكارع والسفرجل والدر والجواهر واللآليء والأدم والجلود والخشب فلا يجوز السلم في شيء منها عدداً للتفاوت إلا إذا ذكر ضابطاً غير مجرد العدد كطول أو غلظ أو غير ذلك. ومن المتفاوت الجوالق والفاء فلا يجوز إلا بذكر مميزات وأجازوه في الباذنجان إلا بالتزام أن الأعمش قائل بانعقاد البيع بلفظ السلم وإلا فيجوز أن يكون قائلاً بمقابل الأصح من أنه لا يجوز وحينئذ فلا يتم المطلوب. واعترضه أيضاً بأن صاحب الثوب وإن أعطاه له بدراهم مؤجلة لكن على أنها مبيعة لا على أنها ثمن ليلزم أن يكون من أفراد البيع وذكر باقي شروط السلم قرينة على إرادة هذا المعنى فتأمل اهـ وأنت خبير بأن كلاً من الاعتراضين ساقط ؛ أما الأول فلأن فرض المسألة أنه أسلم ثوباً مثلاً في دراهم وقد قال أبو بكر الأعمش : إنه ينعقد بيعاً لا سلماً. فهذا صريح بأنه يقول إن البيع ينعقد بلفظ السلم. وقد ذكر في النهر in a weighed item. And he restricted 'muthamman' as a precaution against dirhams and dinars, for even though they are weighed, they are price (thaman), so salam is not permissible in them because salam is the payment of price in advance and delaying the sold item. If it were permissible in them, it would be reversed. So if it does not occur as salam, it is void according to 'Isa ibn Aban. Al-A'mash said it is a sale with deferred price, considering the meaning. The first is more correct because it cannot be validated in other than what the contract was made for. In Fath al-Qadir, al-A'mash's view is preferred as more juristic. This disagreement applies when what is paid in advance is other than prices, like wheat. But if the prices themselves are paid in advance, there is consensus it is not permissible. If one pays in advance for a measured item by weight, e.g., pays in advance for wheat or barley by weight, there are two narrations; the relied-upon is permissibility because precision is achieved. Similarly, if one pays in advance for a weighed item by measure. His statement: (And it is valid in similar countable items like eggs and walnuts because it is known, precise, and deliverable, and any variation is disregarded by custom. There is no dispute about its permissibility by count; the dispute is about by measure. According to us, it is permissible by measure; Zufar prohibited it by measure. It is also narrated that he prohibited it by count due to variation, and we have responded to him. It is only permissible by measure because precision is achieved. It is restricted to 'similar' [items]. Among them are pears, apricots, and figs, as in Furūq al-Karābīsī, because heterogeneous countable items are not valid for salam. Items whose value varies widely, like watermelon, pumpkin, pomegranate, heads, trotters, quince, pearls, gems, precious stones, leather, skins, and wood, salam is not permissible in any of them by count due to variation, unless a different specification is mentioned beyond mere count, like length or thickness. Among heterogeneous items are sacks and [word unclear], so they are not permissible unless with distinguishing features. They permitted it in eggplant [subject to condition]. Except that al-A'mash holds that a sale is concluded with the word 'salam', otherwise it is possible that he holds the opposite of the correct view that it is not permissible, and then the desired conclusion is not reached. He also objected that the owner of the cloth, although he gave it for deferred dirhams, but as a sold item, not as price, so it would be an instance of sale. Mentioning the other conditions of salam is an indication that this meaning is intended, so reflect. And you are aware that both objections are invalid. As for the first, because the scenario is that one pays a cloth, for example, in advance for dirhams, and Abu Bakr al-A'mash said it is concluded as a sale, not salam. This is clear that he says a sale is concluded with the word salam. And it was mentioned in al-Nahr before this that the author of al-Qunyah did not report any disagreement about its conclusion with the word salam. As for the second, because the author of Fath acknowledges that the contract is a salam contract but some of its conditions as a salam are missing, and the word that concludes a sale is found, so the contract becomes a sale contract because both salam and sale share in being an exchange of property for property, and the parties intended it, and there is no legal impediment to this intended exchange, if it is not valid in a specific form they intended, being valid in another form, just as if they intend a partnership contract in the form of muwafada (full partnership) and some of its conditions are missing, it becomes a joint partnership (inan) even if they did not intend that form. There are many similar examples, like if one gives a gift to a poor person or gives charity to a rich person, the first is charity and the second is a gift, and like if one appoints someone as executor during his life or as proxy after his death, the first is a proxy and the second is an executor, and like if...
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This lesson addresses two main issues: first, the ruling on salam in dirhams and dinars (monetary metals). The author explains that these are thaman (price), not muthman (sold item), so salam is not permissible in them because salam requires the price to be paid in advance and the sold item delayed; if you pay money in advance, the opposite would happen (the price becomes delayed). If someone uses dirhams as the subject of salam (i.e., pays a cloth for future delivery of dirhams), the contract would be invalid as salam according to 'Isa ibn Aban. Al-A'mash, however, argues that such a contract should be considered a sale with deferred price (i.e., valid as a sale) by considering the economic reality. Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir prefers al-A'mash's view as more juristic. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq then defends this preference, noting that if the parties used words of salam but conditions for salam are missing, the contract can still be valid as a sale because both contracts are exchanges of property, and there is no legal impediment to reinterpreting it. He gives analogies: a partnership intended as muwafada becoming a joint partnership if conditions fail, a gift to a poor person becoming charity, etc. The second issue is using a different standard for measurement: if one pays in advance for a measured item by weight or a weighed item by measure, the relied-upon view is permissibility as long as precision is achieved. This is based on the principle that the primary goal is avoidance of dispute. Zufar disagreed, but the Hanafi school accepts both methods. The passage then discusses countable items: similar countable items (mutaqarib) like eggs and walnuts are valid by count or by measure, according to the Hanafis (Zufar prohibited by measure). Heterogeneous items (mutafawit) like watermelon, pomegranate, etc., are not valid by count unless additional specifications are provided. The lesson concludes with a detailed refutation of objections against al-A'mash's view, showing that the contract can be valid as a sale if the word of salam is used but conditions are incomplete.

Key Terms
المثمن (al-muthamman): The item being sold (the subject of the sale) as opposed to thaman (price).
الدراهم والدنانير (al-darāhim wa al-danānīr): Silver and gold coins, which serve as price (thaman) in transactions.
السلم (al-salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance and the sold item is delivered later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The contract is void because salam in dirhams is invalid
B) The contract is valid as a sale with deferred price
C) The contract is valid as a salam because the dirhams are considered commodity
D) The contract is suspended until both parties agree

Key Takeaway
When salam in monetary metals fails, the contract can be upheld as a sale because the core intention is exchange.

Salam by Weight, Measure, and Countable Items
Resolves disagreement on salam in monetary metals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mutaqarib and mutafawit countable items and apply the Hanafi rules on salam by alternative measurement standards.

Core Idea
Salam is valid by weight or measure as long as precision is achieved; countable items are valid if similar, but not if highly variable.

Can you pay in advance for wheat by weight even though it's usually sold by measure? What about eggs or watermelons by count? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rules on salam with different measurement standards and the crucial distinction between similar (mutaqarib) and heterogeneous (mutafawit) countable items. We'll also explore Zufar's dissent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the standard for weight/measure flexibility
The relied-upon view is that one can do salam in a measured item (like wheat) by weight, and in a weighed item (like meat) by measure, as long as precision is achieved.
Zufar disagreed; the commentary says there are two narrations from him.
2
Define similar countable items (mutaqarib)
Items like eggs and walnuts are similar in size and value, so variation is ignored by custom. Salam is valid by count or by measure.
No dispute on permissibility by count; dispute on by measure (Zufar prohibited by measure).
3
Define heterogeneous countable items (mutafawit)
Items like watermelons, pomegranates, and heads vary greatly; salam by count alone is invalid. Additional specifications (weight, size) are needed.
The text lists many examples: pearls, gems, leather, wood, etc.
4
Analyze Zufar's objection
Zufar prohibited salam in mutaqarib by measure, and also prohibited it by count in some narrations, citing variation. The Hanafi majority responded that custom disregards minor variation.
The phrase 'وأجبنا عنه' indicates the response is already given in other texts.
5
Apply the rules to new scenarios
Classify any countable item as mutaqarib or mutafawit based on custom, then determine if additional description is needed.
When in doubt, additional specifications are safer to avoid dispute.

قبل هذا أن صاحب القنية لم يحك خلافاً في انعقاده بلفظ السلم. وأما الثاني فلأن صاحب الفتح معترف بأن العقد عقد سلم ولكنه اختل بعض شروطه على أنه سلم ووجد اللفظ الذي ينعقد به البيع فيصير العقد عقد بيع لأن كلاً من السلم والبيع يشتركان في كونهما مبادلة مال بمال وقد قصده المتعاقدان ولا مانع شرعاً من كون هذه المبادلة المقصودة إذا لم تصح على صفة خاصة قصدها المتعاقدان أن تصح على صفة أخرى كما إذا قصدا عقد الشركة على صفة كونها مفاوضة وفقد بعض شروطها فإنها تصير شركة عنان وإن لم يقصدا هذه الصفة، ولذلك نظائر كثيرة كما لو وهب للفقير أو تصدق على غني يكون الأول صدقة والثاني هبة وكما لو أقام غيره وصياً في حياته أو وكيلاً بعد وفاته يكون الأول وكيلاً والثاني وصياً، وكما لو
in a weighed item. And he restricted 'muthamman' as a precaution against dirhams and dinars, for even though they are weighed, they are price (thaman), so salam is not permissible in them because salam is the payment of price in advance and delaying the sold item. If it were permissible in them, it would be reversed. So if it does not occur as salam, it is void according to 'Isa ibn Aban. Al-A'mash said it is a sale with deferred price, considering the meaning. The first is more correct because it cannot be validated in other than what the contract was made for. In Fath al-Qadir, al-A'mash's view is preferred as more juristic. This disagreement applies when what is paid in advance is other than prices, like wheat. But if the prices themselves are paid in advance, there is consensus it is not permissible. If one pays in advance for a measured item by weight, e.g., pays in advance for wheat or barley by weight, there are two narrations; the relied-upon is permissibility because precision is achieved. Similarly, if one pays in advance for a weighed item by measure. His statement: (And it is valid in similar countable items like eggs and walnuts because it is known, precise, and deliverable, and any variation is disregarded by custom. There is no dispute about its permissibility by count; the dispute is about by measure. According to us, it is permissible by measure; Zufar prohibited it by measure. It is also narrated that he prohibited it by count due to variation, and we have responded to him. It is only permissible by measure because precision is achieved. It is restricted to 'similar' [items]. Among them are pears, apricots, and figs, as in Furūq al-Karābīsī, because heterogeneous countable items are not valid for salam. Items whose value varies widely, like watermelon, pumpkin, pomegranate, heads, trotters, quince, pearls, gems, precious stones, leather, skins, and wood, salam is not permissible in any of them by count due to variation, unless a different specification is mentioned beyond mere count, like length or thickness. Among heterogeneous items are sacks and [word unclear], so they are not permissible unless with distinguishing features. They permitted it in eggplant [subject to condition]. Except that al-A'mash holds that a sale is concluded with the word 'salam', otherwise it is possible that he holds the opposite of the correct view that it is not permissible, and then the desired conclusion is not reached. He also objected that the owner of the cloth, although he gave it for deferred dirhams, but as a sold item, not as price, so it would be an instance of sale. Mentioning the other conditions of salam is an indication that this meaning is intended, so reflect. And you are aware that both objections are invalid. As for the first, because the scenario is that one pays a cloth, for example, in advance for dirhams, and Abu Bakr al-A'mash said it is concluded as a sale, not salam. This is clear that he says a sale is concluded with the word salam. And it was mentioned in al-Nahr before this that the author of al-Qunyah did not report any disagreement about its conclusion with the word salam. As for the second, because the author of Fath acknowledges that the contract is a salam contract but some of its conditions as a salam are missing, and the word that concludes a sale is found, so the contract becomes a sale contract because both salam and sale share in being an exchange of property for property, and the parties intended it, and there is no legal impediment to this intended exchange, if it is not valid in a specific form they intended, being valid in another form, just as if they intend a partnership contract in the form of muwafada (full partnership) and some of its conditions are missing, it becomes a joint partnership (inan) even if they did not intend that form. There are many similar examples, like if one gives a gift to a poor person or gives charity to a rich person, the first is charity and the second is a gift, and like if one appoints someone as executor during his life or as proxy after his death, the first is a proxy and the second is an executor, and like if...
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This lesson addresses two main issues: first, the ruling on salam in dirhams and dinars (monetary metals). The author explains that these are thaman (price), not muthman (sold item), so salam is not permissible in them because salam requires the price to be paid in advance and the sold item delayed; if you pay money in advance, the opposite would happen (the price becomes delayed). If someone uses dirhams as the subject of salam (i.e., pays a cloth for future delivery of dirhams), the contract would be invalid as salam according to 'Isa ibn Aban. Al-A'mash, however, argues that such a contract should be considered a sale with deferred price (i.e., valid as a sale) by considering the economic reality. Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir prefers al-A'mash's view as more juristic. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq then defends this preference, noting that if the parties used words of salam but conditions for salam are missing, the contract can still be valid as a sale because both contracts are exchanges of property, and there is no legal impediment to reinterpreting it. He gives analogies: a partnership intended as muwafada becoming a joint partnership if conditions fail, a gift to a poor person becoming charity, etc. The second issue is using a different standard for measurement: if one pays in advance for a measured item by weight or a weighed item by measure, the relied-upon view is permissibility as long as precision is achieved. This is based on the principle that the primary goal is avoidance of dispute. Zufar disagreed, but the Hanafi school accepts both methods. The passage then discusses countable items: similar countable items (mutaqarib) like eggs and walnuts are valid by count or by measure, according to the Hanafis (Zufar prohibited by measure). Heterogeneous items (mutafawit) like watermelon, pomegranate, etc., are not valid by count unless additional specifications are provided. The lesson concludes with a detailed refutation of objections against al-A'mash's view, showing that the contract can be valid as a sale if the word of salam is used but conditions are incomplete.

Key Terms
المثمن (al-muthamman): The item being sold (the subject of the sale) as opposed to thaman (price).
العددي المتقارب (al-ʿadadī al-mutaqārib): Countable items that are similar in size and value, like eggs and walnuts, where minor variation is ignored by custom.
العددي المتفاوت (al-ʿadadī al-mutafāwit): Countable items with significant variation in size and value, like watermelons, requiring additional description beyond count.
الضبط (al-ḍabṭ): Precision or exactness in measurement, which is the basis for allowing salam by alternative standards.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of a mutafawit countable item according to the text?
A) Eggs
B) Walnuts
C) Watermelons
D) Pears

Key Takeaway
Salam is flexible in measurement standards and categorizes countable items as mutaqarib or mutafawit, with mutafawit requiring extra description to avoid gharar.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Transformation of Void Salam into Sale: The Dispute Between 'Isa ibn Aban and al-A'mash
Intra-Hanafi dispute on transformation of void salam into sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the majority Hanafi position on a salam contract in dirhams and dinars when conditions fail, and evaluate al-A'mash's view that it transforms into a deferred sale.

Core Idea
A void salam does not become a sale automatically—a contract's form is specific.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: if a salam contract in dirhams and dinars fails because they are prices, can it be salvaged as a valid sale? The commentator presents the majority view (via 'Isa ibn Aban) that it is void, and al-A'mash's alternative that it becomes a sale with deferred price. Through analogies from partnership, gifts, and agency, the author defends the majority position while acknowledging the appeal of al-A'mash's jurisprudential reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the core issue
Identify the legal question: Can a void salam contract in dirhams and dinars transform into a valid sale?
Dirhams and dinars are normally thaman (price), so salam using them as goods inverts the essence of salam.
2
Identify the two positions
Name the two Hanafi authorities: 'Isa ibn Aban says void; al-A'mash says it becomes a sale with deferred price.
'Isa ibn Aban's view is considered the majority position (al-awwal asahh).
3
Examine each party's reasoning
Explain the dalil of each: 'Isa ibn Aban relies on the specificity of contract forms (salam vs. sale); al-A'mash focuses on the underlying exchange intention.
The text states: 'al-awwal asahh li annahu la yumkinu tas-hihuhu fi ghairi ma awjaba al-'aqdu fih'.
4
Analyze the objections and responses
The commentator refutes two objections from Fath al-Qadir, using analogies from partnership, gifts, and agency to show that contracts can transform when conditions are missing.
Key analogies: muwafadah to 'inan; gift to charity; agent to executor; currency exchange.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon ruling is that the contract is void (batil), though al-A'mash's view is noted for its jurisprudential depth.
In Fath al-Qadir, al-A'mash's view is preferred 'bi annahu adkhalu fi al-fiqh', but the majority holds the first view.

كتاب البيع/ باب السلم في موزون. وقيد المثمن احترازاً عن الدراهم والدنانير فإنه وإن كانت موزونة لكنها ثمن فلا يجوز الإسلام فيها لأن السلم تعجيل الثمن وتأجيل المبيع، ولو جاز فيها انعكس فإذا لم يقع سلماً يكون باطلاً عند عيسى بن أبان. وقال الأعمش بكون بيعاً بثمن مؤجل اعتباراً للمعنى والأول أصح لأنه لا يمكن تصحيحه في غير ما أوجبا العقد فيه. ورجح قول الأعمش في فتح القدير بأنه أدخل في الفقه، وهذا الخلاف فيما إذا أسلم فيهما غير الأثمان كالحنطة، وأما إذا أسلم فيهما الأثمان لم يجز إجماعاً ولو أسلم في المكيل وزناً كما إذا أسلم في البر والشعير بالميزان فيه روايتان والمعتمد الجواز لوجود الضبط وعلى هذا الخلاف لو أسلم في الموزون كيلاً.
قوله: (ويصح في العددي المتقارب كالبيض والجوز لأنه معلوم مضبوط مقدور التسليم وما فيه من التفاوت مهدر عرفاً ولا خلاف في جوازه عدداً إنما الخلاف فيه كيلاً، فعندنا يجوز كيلاً ومنعه زفر كيلاً وعنه منعه والقرع والرمان والرؤوس والأكارع والسفرجل والدر والجواهر واللآليء والأدم والجلود والخشب فلا يجوز السلم في شيء منها عدداً للتفاوت إلا إذا ذكر ضابطاً غير مجرد العدد كطول أو غلظ أو غير ذلك. ومن المتفاوت الجوالق والفاء فلا يجوز إلا بذكر مميزات وأجازوه في الباذنجان إلا بالتزام أن الأعمش قائل بانعقاد البيع بلفظ السلم وإلا فيجوز أن يكون قائلاً بمقابل الأصح من أنه لا يجوز وحينئذ فلا يتم المطلوب. واعترضه أيضاً بأن صاحب الثوب وإن أعطاه له بدراهم مؤجلة لكن على أنها مبيعة لا على أنها ثمن ليلزم أن يكون من أفراد البيع وذكر باقي شروط السلم قرينة على إرادة هذا المعنى فتأمل اهـ وأنت خبير بأن كلاً من الاعتراضين ساقط ؛ أما الأول فلأن فرض المسألة أنه أسلم ثوباً مثلاً في دراهم وقد قال أبو بكر الأعمش : إنه ينعقد بيعاً لا سلماً. فهذا صريح بأنه يقول إن البيع ينعقد بلفظ السلم. وقد ذكر في النهر قبل هذا أن السلم والبيع يشتركان في كونهما مبادلة مال بمال وقد قصده المتعاقدان ولا مانع شرعاً من كون هذه المبادلة المقصودة إذا لم تصح على صفة خاصة قصدها المتعاقدان أن تصح على صفة أخرى كما إذا قصدا عقد الشركة على صفة كونها مفاوضة وفقد بعض شروطها فإنها تصير شركة عنان وإن لم يقصدا هذه الصفة، ولذلك نظائر كثيرة كما لو وهب للفقير أو تصدق على غني يكون الأول صدقة والثاني هبة وكما لو أقام غيره وصياً في حياته أو وكيلاً بعد وفاته يكون الأول وكيلاً والثاني وصياً، وكما لو اشترى أمة تعدل ألف درهم مع طوق فضة قيمته ألف درهم ونقد من الثمن ألفاً فهو ثمن الفضة، سواء سكت أو قال خذ هذا من ثمنها تحرياً للجواز كما سيأتي في الصرف، ولا يخفى أن تحري الجواز في مسألتنا بالأولى لأنه لم يصرح فيها بخلاف الجائز، وإن صرح فهي مثل مسألة الصرف فتأمل منصفاً.
قوله : (وشرط في الخلاصة ذكر المكان الخ أقول : عبارة الخلاصة هكذا: ولا بأس بالسلم في اللبن والآجر إذا بين الملبن والمكان وذكر عدداً معلوماً والمكان. قال بعضهم: مكان الإيفاء هذا قول أبي حنيفة . وقال بعضهم المكان الذي يضرب فيه اللبن انتهت فكان ينبغي يذكر قول الإمام ولا سيما مع احتمال أن يكون ذلك البعض من غير أهل المذهب.
قوله: (والملبن والكاغد عدداً لإهدار التفاوت. وفي فتح القدير : وفيه نظر ظاهر أو بحمل على كاغد بقالب خاص وإلا فلا يجوز وكون الباذنجان مهدر التفاوت لعله في باذنجان ديارهم وفي ديارنا ليس كذلك بخلاف بيض النعام وجوز الهند لا يستحق شيء منه بالإسلام بخلاف بيض الدجاج والجوز الشامي والفرنجي لعدم إهدار التفاوت. ويشترط مع العدد بيان الصفة أيضاً في شرح الشافي فلو أسلم في بيض النعام أو في جوز الهند جاز كما جاز في الأخيرين، وعن أبي حنيفة أنه عدداً منعه في بيض النعام ادعاء للتفاوت في المالية وهو خلاف ظاهر الرواية. والوجه أن ينظر إلى الغرض في عرف الناس ؛ فإن كان الغرض في ذلك العرف حصول القشر ليتخذ في سلاسل القناديل كما في ديار مصر وغيرها من الأمصار يجب أن نقاء يعمل بهذه الرواية فلا يجوز السلم فيها بعد ذكر العدد إلا مع تعيين المقدار واللون من البياض أو إهداره اهـ . وفي المعراج والفاصل بين المتفاوت والمتقارب أن ما ضمن مستهلكه بالمثل فهو متقارب وبالقيمة يكون متفاوتاً. وفي البزازية : يجوز السلم في الأواني المتخذة . الخزف عدداً إن نوعاً يصير معلوماً عند الناس، ويجوز في الكيزان الخزفية إذا بين نوع لا يتفاوت آحاده اهـ. ولم يشترط المؤلف للجواز إعلام الصفة أنه جيد أو وسط أو رديء ومنهم من شرط أعلام الصفة؛ كذا في الذخيرة وفيها عن أبي يوسف : لو أسلم بيض الأوز في بيض الدجاج أو أسلم بيض النعام في بيض الدجاج جاز، وإن أسلم بيض الدجاج في بيض نعامة أو أسلم بيض الدجاج في بيض الأوز ؛ وإن كان في حين يقدر عليه جاز، فإن كان في حين لا يقدر عليه لا يجوز اهـ .
من قوله : (والفلس) لأنه عددي يمكن ضبطه فيصح السلم فيه ، وقيل لا يصح عند محمد العد لأنه ثمن ما دام يروج وظاهر الرواية عن الكل الجواز. وإذا بطلت ثمنيتها لا يخرج عن إلى الوزن للعرف إلا أن يهدره أهل العرف كما هو في زماننا فإن الفلوس أثمان في زماننا ولا تقبل إلا وزناً فلا يجوز السلم فيها إلا وزناً في ديارنا في زماننا، وقد كانت قبل هذه الأعصار عددية في ديارنا أيضاً؛ كذا في فتح القدير قوله : ((واللبن) بكسر الباء وهو الطوب . ولا بأس بالسلم في اللبن والآجر إذا بين الملبن والمكان وذكر عدداً معلوماً والمكان.
Book of Sales/Chapter of Salam. In weighed items. And the restriction of the price (al-muthaman) is to exclude dirhams and dinars, for although they are weighed, they are price (thaman), so salam in them is not permissible because salam is advancing the price and deferring the sold item. If it were permissible in them, it would be reversed. So if it does not occur as salam, it is void according to 'Isa ibn Aban. And al-A'mash said it becomes a sale with deferred price, considering the meaning. And the first is more correct because it cannot be validated in other than what the contract parties intended. And in Fath al-Qadir, al-A'mash's view is preferred as more jurisprudential. This dispute is when salam is done in them (dirhams/dinars) as non-price items like wheat. But if one does salam in them as price items, it is not permissible by consensus. And if one does salam in measured items by weight, like salam in wheat and barley by weight, there are two narrations, and the relied-upon is permissibility due to the existence of precision. And similarly, if one does salam in weighed items by measure.
He said: (And it is valid in close countable items like eggs and walnuts) because they are known, precise, and capable of delivery, and any variation is disregarded customarily. There is no dispute about its permissibility by count; the dispute is by measure. According to us, it is permissible by measure, but Zufar prohibits it by measure. And from him also a prohibition by count due to variation, and we answered him. It is only permissible by measure because precision exists. And the restriction to closeness includes pears, apricots, and figs, as in the furuq of al-Karabisi, because distant countable items are not permissible in salam. And what has varied in its value, like watermelon, pumpkin, pomegranate, heads, trotters, quince, pearls, jewels, gems, leather, skins, and wood, salam in any of them by count is not permissible due to variation, unless a specification other than mere count is mentioned, like length or thickness or other. Among the distant items are sacks and ... so it is not permissible unless with distinguishing features. And they permitted it in eggplant only by accepting that al-A'mash holds the contract of sale with the word salam; otherwise it may be that he holds the opposite of the correct view that it is not permissible, and then the desired result is not achieved. And he also objected that the owner of the cloth, although he gave it to him for deferred dirhams, but on the basis that they are sold, not that they are price, so it would be an instance of sale, and mentioning the remaining conditions of salam is a presumption for intending this meaning, so reflect. And you are aware that both objections are invalid. As for the first, because the premise of the issue is that he did salam in a cloth, for example, for dirhams, and Abu Bakr al-A'mash said that it becomes a sale, not a salam. This is explicit that he says the sale is concluded with the word salam. And it was mentioned in al-Nahr before this that the author of al-Qunyah did not relate a dispute about its conclusion with the word salam. As for the second, because the author of Fath acknowledges that the contract is a salam contract but some of its conditions as salam were missing, and the word that concludes a sale is found, so the contract becomes a sale contract, because both salam and sale share in being an exchange of property for property, and the two parties intended it, and there is no legal impediment to this intended exchange, if it does not validate as a specific form intended by the parties, that it validates as another form, like if they intended a partnership contract as a muwafadah and some of its conditions are missing, it becomes an 'inan partnership even if they did not intend this form. And there are many analogies to that, like if one gifts to a poor person or gives charity to a rich person, the first is charity and the second is a gift, and like if one appoints another as executor during his life or as agent after his death, the first is an agent and the second is an executor, and like if one buys a slave girl valued at a thousand dirhams with a silver necklace valued at a thousand dirhams and pays a thousand dirhams as the price, it is the price of the silver, whether he remains silent or says 'take this from its price', seeking validity as will come in currency exchange. And it is not hidden that seeking validity in our issue is even more so, because he did not explicitly state anything contrary to the valid, and if he did, it is like the currency exchange issue, so reflect fairly.
He said: (And the condition in al-Khulasa is to mention the place, etc.) I say: The expression of al-Khulasa is as follows: There is no harm in salam in bricks and baked bricks if the place of making bricks and the location are specified, and a known number and the place are mentioned. Some said: The place of delivery is the saying of Abu Hanifa. And some said the place where the bricks are made. End. So he should have mentioned the Imam's saying, especially since that someone may be from outside the school.
He said: (And the brick and paper by count due to disregard of variation. And in Fath al-Qadir: There is apparent doubt in it, or it is interpreted as paper with a specific mold, otherwise it is not permissible. And that eggplant has disregarded variation is perhaps in their region, but in our region it is not so, unlike ostrich eggs and coconuts, nothing is entitled from them by salam, unlike chicken eggs and Syrian and Frankish walnuts, due to lack of disregard of variation. And it is required along with count to mention the quality also, as in Sharh al-Shafi. So if one does salam in ostrich eggs or coconuts, it is permissible as it is permissible in the latter two. And from Abu Hanifa that by count he prohibited it in ostrich eggs claiming variation in value, which is contrary to the zahir al-riwaya. And the correct approach is to consider the customary purpose; if the purpose in that custom is to obtain the shell to make into lamp chains, as in Egypt and other regions, then it is necessary to act on this narration, so salam in them is not permissible after mentioning the count unless specifying the quantity and color of whiteness or disregard. End. And in al-Mi'raj: The distinction between distant and close is that what is guaranteed by its equivalent in case of destruction is close, and by value is distant. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: Salam is permissible in utensils made of pottery by count if the type becomes known to people, and it is permissible in pottery mugs if the type is specified such that individual pieces do not vary. End. And the author did not require for validity the indication of quality (good, medium, or poor), and some required indication of quality; as in al-Dhakhira, and in it from Abu Yusuf: If one does salam in goose eggs for chicken eggs, or does salam in ostrich eggs for chicken eggs, it is permissible. And if one does salam in chicken eggs for ostrich eggs, or does salam in chicken eggs for goose eggs, if at a time when they are available, it is permissible; if at a time when they are not available, it is not permissible. End.
From his saying: (And the fals) because it is countable and can be precisely specified, so salam in it is valid. And it is said it is not valid according to Muhammad due to it being a price as long as it circulates. And the apparent narration from all is permissibility. And if its price-ness ceases, it does not exit to weight unless the custom treats it as such, except if custom disregards it as is in our time, for fals are prices in our time and are only accepted by weight, so salam in them is not permissible except by weight in our region in our time, and before these times they were countable in our region as well. As in Fath al-Qadir. His saying: (And al-labn) with kasra on the ba, meaning bricks. And there is no harm in salam in bricks and baked bricks if the place of making bricks and the location are specified, and a known number and the place are mentioned.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a detailed commentary on the chapter of salam from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It addresses two main issues: the validity of salam in dirhams and dinars, and the permissibility of salam in countable items. The text begins by stating that salam in dirhams and dinars is invalid because they are typically used as prices (thaman) not as goods (muthaman). There is a key intra-Hanafi dispute: 'Isa ibn Aban holds such a contract void if conditions of salam are unmet, while al-A'mash argues it becomes a valid sale with deferred price. The commentator notes that in Fath al-Qadir, al-A'mash's view is preferred but that the majority follow the first opinion. He then discusses an objection about a cloth exchanged for deferred dirhams, and provides a detailed refutation using analogies from partnership, gifts, and agency to show that contracts can transform when conditions fail, provided the exchange nature is preserved. The second major section deals with countable items. Items that are 'muttaqarib' (similar in units) like eggs and walnuts are valid for salam by count or measure, as variation is negligible. Items that are 'mutafawit' (dissimilar) like watermelons or precious stones are not valid by count alone unless additional specifications (size, weight, color) are given. The text then addresses specific items: eggplant, paper, bricks, and fals (copper coins). For fals, the ruling depends on custom: if they circulate as prices, salam in them is invalid by count but may be valid by weight. For bricks, the place of manufacture and delivery must be specified according to Abu Hanifa. Throughout, the commentator cites multiple sources (al-Karabisi, Fath al-Qadir, al-Bazzaziyya, al-Dhakhira, etc.) and presents differences among Hanafi scholars, including Zufar, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. The final part emphasizes that custom ('urf) plays a crucial role in determining whether variation is disregarded.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A contract of advance payment for deferred delivery of specified goods.
مثمن (muthaman): The goods sold in a contract (the object of sale), as opposed to the price (thaman).
ثمن (thaman): The price given in exchange for goods; typically dirhams and dinars in classical fiqh.
باطل (batil): Void ab initio; the contract has no legal effect and must be rescinded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling on a salam contract in dirhams and dinars if the conditions of salam are not met?
A) The contract is void (batil).
B) The contract becomes a valid sale with deferred price.
C) The contract is fasid (voidable) and can be corrected.
D) The contract is valid as a salam because dirhams are weighed.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a void salam does not automatically become a sale; the contract is void unless the parties explicitly intended a different form of exchange.
